(2) **Marketplace checkout/license purchase** — `studio_voice_clone_licenses` + the access check exist and are honored, but there is NO buy/checkout route that CREATES a license (95/5 split, CC-on-buyer per PRD §6); listing a clone as `marketplace` works, purchasing one does not. (3) **Provenance/moderation (§5 GA gate)** — consent attestation is enforced on create, but provenance disclosure on listings, the moderation gate on publish, and an audio watermark are not built. (4) **G2P + WGSL** — char-level tokenizer (no phonemizer) and CPU SSM scan (no WebGPU Mamba kernel). (5) **LLM-flow wiring (#1995/#1997)** — script→narration / dubbing / pitch surfaces don't yet route their text through the narration seam (those studio UIs aren't in the repo).

- **Voice-clone foundation (Phase 1 + 2) shipped into `@seanhogg/builderforce-studio`; trained weights + the server synthesize route are the open seams.** Built the in-browser, weight-free, device-routed clone stack under [studio/src/engine/voice](studio/src/engine/voice): Phase 1 — shared DSP ([audio-frames.ts](studio/src/engine/voice/audio-frames.ts): FFT, mel filterbank, mel→PCM vocoder), the x-vector-style [speaker-encoder.ts](studio/src/engine/voice/speaker-encoder.ts) (stats-pooled identity embedding), and the RVQ [neural-codec.ts](studio/src/engine/voice/neural-codec.ts) (PCM↔discrete tokens); Phase 2 — the SSM [ssm-acoustic-model.ts](studio/src/engine/voice/ssm-acoustic-model.ts) ((text+speaker)→codec tokens on the same `h_{t+1}=A·h_t+B·x_t` recurrence as [mamba-coherence.ts](studio/src/engine/mamba-coherence.ts), Cartesia's SSM-over-codec bet), the [voice-clone-engine.ts](studio/src/engine/voice/voice-clone-engine.ts) orchestrator (device-routed via the shared `probeDevice`), and the swappable [provider.ts](studio/src/engine/voice/provider.ts) seam. 28 voice tests green; studio builds ESM/CJS/DTS. **#1994 (server synthesize): NOW SHIPPED** — `POST /api/studio/voice-clones/:id/synthesize` + the `studio_voice_clones`/`studio_voice_clone_licenses`/`studio_voiceovers` tables + the full route family exist (see the "#1994 server backend SHIPPED" entry above; migration 0127). **Residual (weights):** the encoder/codec/acoustic models are deterministic seeded *reference* implementations — correct shapes, conditioning, and streaming recurrence, but **placeholder weights**, so output is structured voice-/text-dependent acoustic texture, not intelligible speech. Intelligibility needs the Phase 2 *training* run (codec + speaker encoder + SSM acoustic model on a licensed multi-speaker corpus); trained matrices drop in behind the identical interfaces (`NeuralCodecOptions.codebooks`, `AcousticWeights`). **Residual (G2P):** [text-tokenizer.ts](studio/src/engine/voice/text-tokenizer.ts) is char-level; a grapheme→phoneme front-end drops in behind `tokenizeText` without touching the acoustic model. **Residual (WGSL):** the SSM scan runs on the CPU Float32 fallback; the WebGPU Mamba kernel (same gap as the diffusion-coherence WGSL kernel above) makes the on-device path fast. Fixing #1994 is the highest-leverage next step — it makes the marketing claim true on every device.

- **`@seanhogg/builderforce-voice` npm package shipped (client seam); it is the consumer contract for hired.video, ahead of the server it calls.** New publishable package at [voice/](voice) (tsup dual ESM/CJS, 13 tests green): `resolveNarrationEngine()` / `VoiceClient` pick the on-device clone (free, WebGPU) → metered server (`ServerCloneProvider`) → honest named-voice fallback, with `getEngineUnavailableReason` as the single source of truth for the "can I clone now" UI (PRD §4 + §7). The on-device path is structurally typed against the studio engine so `@seanhogg/builderforce-studio` stays an optional peer. **Residual:** the `ServerCloneProvider` calls the #1994 endpoint that doesn't exist yet, so only the on-device and fallback paths run end-to-end today; and the four LLM creation flows (script→narration, dubbing panel, value-prop/pitch, calibration read-script — PRD §4 #1995/#1997) are **not yet wired** to route their generated text through this seam (those studio UI surfaces aren't in the repo). Wiring them once the studio UI + #1994 land unblocks "the AI wrote it and it speaks in my voice" across every studio format.

### 🧹 Open — Internal / reliability & tech-debt (73 → ~20 closed 2026-06-21; remainder is blocked: secret-rotation · GPU/browser-verify · Neon-CI · npm-auth · lint-refactor · mega-features — see closeout entry below)

_Refactors, dead-code, unapplied migrations, schema drift, tests, lint, CI, secret hygiene, brand/rename debt, dependency & build plumbing._

- **🔓 agent-runtime plugin-sdk DTS build broken — `tsc -p tsconfig.plugin-sdk.dts.json` emits 9× TS6059 (2026-06-27).** The plugin-sdk declaration-emit step pulls `@builderforce/agent-tools` *source* into its program because that package is source-only (`exports`/`types` → `./src/index.ts`, no dist/.d.ts), and those `packages/agent-tools/src/*.ts` files fall outside the dts tsconfig's `rootDir: "src"`. **Not caused by the TS upgrade** — fails identically on 5.9.3 and 6.0.3 (confirmed by revert test); entangled with concurrent edits to `packages/agent-tools` (new `spec.ts` + `index.ts` re-exports added mid-session) that expand the traversed surface. `tsdown` (main bundle) builds fine; only the standalone `tsc` dts step breaks. `preserveSymlinks` makes it worse (breaks pnpm @types resolution). Fix needs an architectural decision by the agent-tools owner: give `@builderforce/agent-tools` a real `.d.ts` build and split export conditions (`types`→dist `.d.ts`, `import`/`default`→`src` so tsdown still bundles source), OR rework the plugin-sdk dts emit to consume prebuilt declarations. Unblocks: agent-runtime full `pnpm run build` + publishable plugin-sdk types under TS6.

- 🔄 **TECH-DEBT CLOSEOUT — 2026-06-21 (operator confirmed all commits + live-DB migrations deploy).** A focused 3-agent pass + reconciliation against this list. **Verification (whole repo):** api `tsc` clean + **1164 tests green** (+23), frontend `tsc` clean (src) + **286 green**, `check:schema` / `check:migrations` / `check:tracks` all pass; new migrations are files (apply on deploy). - **Agent-execution telemetry now has unit coverage on the discrete WRITERS, but the full-LOOP wiring is still integration-only (2026-06-14).** Added [`cloudTelemetry.test.ts`](api/src/application/runtime/cloudTelemetry.test.ts) (8 tests — drives the real `recordCloudToolEvent`/`recordCloudUsage`/`emitModelSelection`/`emitCodingModelDegraded` against a fake `Db`, asserting `tool_audit_events` rows are keyed `exec:<id>` with cloud attribution, that usage dual-writes `usage_snapshots` AND `llm_usage_log` with the `engine:'cloud'` marker + ticket/project rollup, and that each writer is best-effort/never-throws) and [`workflow-telemetry.test.ts`](agent-runtime/src/infra/workflow-telemetry.test.ts) (9 tests — on-prem `WorkflowTelemetryService` populates all three sinks per span: the day's JSONL audit file, the Builderforce workflow/task REST + OTel `/api/telemetry/spans` HTTP sync with `Authorization`/`X-AgentHost-Id`/`X-Trace-Id` headers, and the live relay hook; covers task token/cost metrics, the `task.fail` path, trace-id lifecycle, local-only no-sync, and throw-isolation). To make the cloud writers testable, three module-private helpers in `cloudAgentEngine.ts` were `export`ed (no behavior change). **Boundary / defensive coverage ADDED 2026-06-14:** `cloudTelemetry.test.ts` (+6) injects wrong/hostile values and proves the best-effort contract — a circular `detail` (JSON.stringify throws) records nothing but never throws, a dead `Db` on BOTH usage ledgers never throws, an unknown plan + blank model still emits a planning row, and `emitCodingModelDegraded` is a strict no-op for junk/sentinel models (no false alarm); [`cloudDispatch.test.ts`](api/src/application/runtime/cloudDispatch.test.ts) (+6) feeds every untrusted-payload reader (`parseModel`/`parseCloudAgentRef`/`parseRepoId`/`parseRemediation`/`markReaperRequeued`/`wasReaperRequeued`/`withDefaultModel`) non-JSON garbage + `'null'` (the `JSON.parse('null')===null` sharp edge) + wrong-type values, asserting safe defaults (undefined/null/unchanged) over a throw; `workflow-telemetry.test.ts` (+4) proves a non-numeric `agentNodeId` skips the numeric OTel proxy but still REST-syncs, a rejecting `fetch` never blocks the JSONL audit, and an invalid `startedAt` (NaN duration → JSON `null`) still records. **DATA-QUALITY GAP — ✓ FIXED 2026-06-14:** bad token counts can no longer reach the billing ledger. Added a shared [`clampTokenCount`](api/src/application/llm/usageLedger.ts) + `sanitizeUsage` in the canonical usage module (floors NaN/Infinity/negative to 0, truncates fractions, preserves cache-field absence) and applied it at the ONE canonical write boundary `recordUsageRow` (so it covers `llm_usage_log` for BOTH the gateway and cloud surfaces, and the priced cost) plus the cloud-only direct `usage_snapshots` write in `recordCloudUsage` — so `SUM(total_tokens)`/cost rollups can be trusted without a downstream sanitize pass. Covered by [usageLedger.test.ts](api/src/application/llm/usageLedger.test.ts) (+9 clamp/sanitize edge cases) and the cloudTelemetry boundary test now asserts NaN/-3 tokens land as `0` in both ledgers. (The `exec:NaN` sessionKey for a degenerate executionId is intentionally left as-is — it is a non-numeric *string* key, not a numeric aggregate column, so it cannot poison any SUM; it merely tags an unattributable event, the correct degraded behavior.) **STILL DEFERRED (needs a mocked gateway/SDK + DB harness, no unit coverage today):** (1) the cloud `runCloudToolLoop`/`runCloudExecution` END-TO-END emission — that a multi-step run with a mocked gateway response actually fires `model.select` once on turn 1, an `llm.complete` + usage row per turn, and `run.failed` on terminal failure (today only the discrete writers are asserted, not that the loop calls them in order); (2) the on-prem relay's `persistToolAudit` + `reportExecutionState` (private `fetch` methods on `BuilderforceRelayService`) and the `runV2Engine` SDK-event→tool-audit SINK mapping (`onAssistantText`→`category:'message'`, `onToolUse`→tool-audit) — the actual on-prem execution→telemetry bridge — remain integration-only; testing them needs the private methods lifted to an injectable seam or the service constructed against a fetch mock. Closing both unblocks a regression guard on the "a run silently produces no timeline/no cost row" failure mode (the exact symptom of execution #59).

- **Engine consolidation — code-quality residue after the `builderforce-local` deletion (2026-06-14).** Operator decision §5.5(a) of [11-prd-engine-consolidation.md](specs/builderforce/11-prd-engine-consolidation.md) retired `builderforce-local`: the unselectable Node shared-registry engine (`LocalAgentEngine`, `node-capability-provider`, `buildNodeToolRegistry`, the 14 duplicate `build*ToolDef` `ToolDefinition` wrappers, `ENGINE_IDS.local`, orphaned `createNodeWebSearch`, and the dormant V1 `pendingTaskRun`/`flushPendingTaskChanges`) was deleted — collapsing an engine-introduced DRY violation (each service tool had been defined twice, once as `AgentTool`, once as `ToolDefinition`). The `run*` pure backends + native `create*Tool` `AgentTool`s (the live on-prem path) stay; all 4 packages `tsc` 0, focused suites green. **Code-review findings — CLOSED 2026-06-14:** (2) the vestigial `_resolved` param on `resolveAgentEngine` was dropped + doc clarified that exactly one engine is reachable from the in-Worker loop (surface routing lives in `runtimeRoutes.ts`, not engine selection); (4) the in-Worker loop and the container `op==='llm'` handler now share one `recordCloudLlmTurn(result, ...)` helper (metering + `llm.complete`/coding-degraded/`agent.message` telemetry) + a `parseLlmChoice` parser — the per-turn LLM step is no longer two copies kept in lockstep; (10) container `repo.edit` omission documented as INTENTIONAL (the image edits in its local clone via shell and delegates only the whole-file commit via the `write` op; advertising `repo.edit` without an `edit` container-op would 400); (14) added a typed `parseModel(payload)` beside `cloudDispatch.ts`'s other `parse*` helpers, reused at both cloudAgentEngine read sites + `withDefaultModel`; (1, partial) the relay's `infra/agent-engine.ts` interface was renamed `AgentEngine`→**`RelayTaskEngine`** + documented as a distinct ORCHESTRATION layer (owns workspace/commit/report) vs the shared pure-loop `@builderforce/agent-tools` `AgentEngine` — the name collision is gone. **Still deferred:** (1, full) actually *collapsing* `RelayTaskEngine` onto the shared `AgentEngine` (reshape `runV2Engine` to `run(input) → AgentRunResult` and lift the ticket-workspace/commit/push/execution-report orchestration out into `dispatchTaskFromRelay`) — a live-dispatch refactor with no unit coverage, so left as a distinct gated step. The **cloud V1 dispatch branch** (`isV2===false` else-path in `runtimeRoutes.ts ~L430` + `cloudAgentTypeLabel`'s V1 arm) remains deploy-gated: un-migrated `engine='builderforce-v1'` rows still reach it until migration `0120` runs live, so it must be removed only after a cloud trace + deploy.

- **Unified Agent Engine — engine seam CONVERGED (Phase A done 2026-06-14); tool-layer reuse REDESIGNED after a hardening-superset finding.** Validation of the Agent Engine seam (PRD [12](specs/builderforce/12-prd-unified-agent-engine.md)) found three *separate* loops: (1) **cloud** `CloudToolLoopEngine`/`runCloudToolLoop` consumes the shared `@builderforce/agent-tools` registry via `CapabilityProvider`; (2) **on-prem TASK** (`runV2Engine`→`claude-agent-sdk-runner.ts`) ran the Claude SDK's own 6 built-ins inline; (3) **on-prem SESSION** (`embedded-runner/run/attempt.ts`) runs ~40 native `AgentTool`s. **DONE this pass (Phase A):** on-prem now implements the SAME shared `AgentEngine` contract cloud does — new [`infra/sdk-agent-engine.ts`](agent-runtime/src/infra/sdk-agent-engine.ts) `ClaudeSdkAgentEngine` wraps the SDK runner and `runV2Engine` drives it via `run(input)→AgentRunResult`; a V3 is now a sibling `AgentEngine` (mirrors cloud `resolveAgentEngine`). `tsgo` 0; 3 unit tests + 826 infra tests green (the lone `gateway-lock.test.ts` failure is a pre-existing env/lock collision, unrelated). No tool-layer/TUI change. **CRITICAL FINDING (rescopes the tool work):** the on-prem native session tools ([`agents/coding-tools.ts`](agent-runtime/src/agents/coding-tools.ts)) are NOT duplicates of the thin shared `core-tools` — they carry sandbox variants, workspace guards, per-provider schema normalization, model-context-scaled read budgets, image sanitization, `apply_patch`, background-process mgmt, owner-only/subagent policy pipelines, before-tool-call hooks, and abort wrapping. The original Phase B ("delete native defs, use the shared registry") would REGRESS that hardening. **Phase D DONE (2026-06-14):** shared `resolveEngineById(registry,id,default?)` in `@builderforce/agent-tools` engine.ts; BOTH seams use it — relay `resolveEngine` AND cloud `resolveAgentEngine` (now an id-keyed factory registry) — so a V3 is one registry entry on either surface, via the same helper. `agent-runtime` tsgo 0 + `api` tsc 0; 4 resolver tests green. (The `toolsFor`/`toolsForCapabilities` "drift" was actually thin already-DRY delegations — not collapsed.) **Prereq resolutions (2026-06-14):** gating = capability (machine) vs policy (caller) are ORTHOGONAL layers, keep both — encoded in `capabilities.ts` (not a blocker); streaming `ctx.onUpdate?` DEFERRED (no consumer until exec/process converge). **NEW gap:** shared `RepoReadCapability.readFile` is text-only → converging `read_file` would lose native image-reading; the read capability needs a media affordance first (read stays native until then). **Phase B tool-CONTRACT convergence LANDED for the file subset (2026-06-14, operator "close the blocker").** Built [`buildNodeCapabilityProvider`](agent-runtime/src/agents/node-capability-provider.ts) (disk twin of cloud `buildCloudProvider`: guarded list/read/`runCodebaseSearch` + mkdir-p write / BOM-CRLF-tolerant unique edit / no-op-on-missing delete, every path workspace-root-guarded) and gave [`registryToAgentTools`](agent-runtime/src/builderforce/agent-loop/tool-adapter.ts) a PRODUCTION caller via [`buildConvergedFileTools`](agent-runtime/src/agents/converged-coding-tools.ts) — shared `write_file`/`edit_file` exposed under the NATIVE names `write`/`edit` (model-facing contract + `tool-display.json` keys unchanged), plus additive `delete_file`/`list_files`. Wired into `createBuilderForceAgentsCodingTools` behind config opt-in `tools.fs.convergedFileTools` (default OFF, NON-sandboxed only), folded in BEFORE the existing normalize/hook/abort/policy pipeline so the hardening is preserved. `tsgo` 0, `oxlint` 0, 25 tests green; default path byte-unchanged. **REMAINING (live gate now a flag flip, not a code blocker):** (1) an owner-run cross-provider smoke test (Anthropic-OAuth/OpenAI/Gemini) that the model drives the converged tools as well as native, then flip `tools.fs.convergedFileTools` ON by default; (2) a sandbox-aware Node provider (fs-bridge backed) so sandboxed sessions converge too; (3) converge `read` (needs a shared read-capability media affordance — text-only today, would lose native image-reading) + `exec`/`process` (needs streaming `ctx.onUpdate?`); (4) `search_code` left native (the on-prem `codebase_search` would otherwise double); Phase C — drive the SDK task runner's tools through the shared registry. Full plan: [PRD 12](specs/builderforce/12-prd-unified-agent-engine.md) §5/§9. Fixing unblocks one drop-in V3 engine + one tool definition per tool on every surface. Flow diagram + end-to-end/divergence assessment: [12a](specs/builderforce/12a-unified-agent-engine-flow.md).

- **Converged on-prem `write`/`edit` narrow file scope to the workspace root (vs native's opt-in guard) — verify before the default-on flip.** Surfaced by the [12a flow assessment](specs/builderforce/12a-unified-agent-engine-flow.md) §3.3: the shared `write_file`/`edit_file` contract is repo/workspace-relative by design, so [`buildNodeCapabilityProvider`](agent-runtime/src/agents/node-capability-provider.ts) unconditionally rejects out-of-workspace paths, whereas native `write`/`edit` allow absolute paths outside the root unless `tools.fs.workspaceOnly` is set. A non-sandboxed session that today writes outside its workspace (legacy `workspaceOnly=false`) loses that once `tools.fs.convergedFileTools` is enabled — a (safer) behavior NARROWING, not a break. Fixing/confirming (decide whether the converged provider should honor a non-guarded mode when `workspaceOnly=false`, or keep always-guarded as the intended hardening) unblocks: a clean default-on flip with no surprise scope regression for out-of-workspace writers.

- **Engine consolidation: retire V1 entirely, collapse to one surface-agnostic V2 engine with FULL capability parity on every surface (local / container / durable) — no reduced tool set anywhere (operator decision, 2026-06-13).** Today three divergent tool sets encode the same branching in three places — `CLOUD_AGENT_TOOLS` (7), `CONTAINER_AGENT_TOOLS` (8), and the local `pi-coding-agent` set (~40 tools) in [agent-runtime/src/agents/pi-tools.ts](agent-runtime/src/agents/pi-tools.ts)+[builderforce-tools.ts](agent-runtime/src/agents/builderforce-tools.ts) — and On-Prem (Hosted) still runs the legacy V1 pi loop ([builderforce-relay.ts](agent-runtime/src/infra/builderforce-relay.ts) `runV1Engine`) instead of V2. V1 has **no remaining unique capability**: the V2 cloud loop already drives the vendor-neutral `CODING_MODEL_POOL` via the OpenAI-shaped `proxy.complete()` and needs no tenant Anthropic key (the "V2 requires BYO key" premise is false — see [anthropicMessagesBridge.ts](api/src/application/llm/anthropicMessagesBridge.ts)). The work: **(1) CapabilityProvider refactor — ✓ SHIPPED 2026-06-13 (keystone).** The three divergent tool lists AND the ~160-line per-tool dispatch `if/else` in `runCloudToolLoop` are replaced by ONE capability-gated registry. A new runtime-agnostic shared package [`@builderforce/agent-tools`](packages/agent-tools/) (no `node:*`, no Worker `Env`, no `pi-agent-core` — bundles under both `moduleResolution: bundler` and `NodeNext`) defines the contract: `ToolDefinition` (OpenAI schema + `requires: Capability[]` + `execute(args, ctx)`), the `Capability` set (`repo.read`/`repo.search`/`repo.write`/`repo.delete`/`shell`/`process`/`static-check`/`human`/`memory`/`web`/`orchestrate`/`message`/`media`), `CapabilityProvider` (the surface's service bag), `ToolRegistry` (filters tools per surface BY capability — `CLOUD_AGENT_TOOLS`/`CONTAINER_AGENT_TOOLS` are now DERIVED and byte-stable, not hand-maintained), the `AgentEngine` DI seam, and the 9 core tool DEFINITIONS ([core-tools.ts](packages/agent-tools/src/core-tools.ts)) so the SAME objects run on every surface. `api` consumes it: [cloudAgentTools.ts](api/src/application/runtime/cloudAgentTools.ts) is now just the two cloud capability SETS + derived schema arrays + step budgets; [cloudAgentEngine.ts](api/src/application/runtime/cloudAgentEngine.ts) adds `buildCloudProvider` (git-API repo read/write/delete + shell-free static-check + approvals-queue human, owning the write/delete bookkeeping) and dispatches via `cloudToolRegistry.dispatch`, with `CloudToolLoopEngine`/`resolveAgentEngine` the injectable engine seam wired at `runCloudExecution` (the finish honesty + anti-stub gates and the ask_human pause stay loop policy, fed by tool `control` signals). `agent-runtime` ALSO consumes it: [buildNodeCapabilityProvider](agent-runtime/src/builderforce/shared-tools/node-capability-provider.ts) (disk + REAL shell, path-escape-guarded) + a [pi-tool adapter](agent-runtime/src/builderforce/shared-tools/pi-tool-adapter.ts) run the same cloud tool definitions on-prem — proven by [pi-tool-adapter.test.ts](agent-runtime/src/builderforce/shared-tools/pi-tool-adapter.test.ts) (write/read/list via disk; run_command via shell; capability gating; root-escape block). Both packages type-check; api type-check + 682 tests green + wrangler `--dry-run` bundle resolves the alias; agent-runtime type-check + the cross-runtime test green. Wiring: tsconfig `paths` in both consumers (tsc + esbuild) plus a vitest resolve-alias in each (vitest ignores tsconfig paths). **Residual tail of (1):** 12 tools are shared `ToolDefinition`s now (the original 9 + `edit_file`/`web_fetch`/`web_search` added 2026-06-13 — full per-tool classification in the dedicated catalogue-completion entry below); the rest of the on-prem pi set (~25: browser, orchestrate/sub-agents, fleet, memory/knowledge-loop, channels [Slack/Discord/Telegram/WhatsApp], image/tts/canvas, sessions, cron, gateway, nodes) are NOT yet ported; the On-Prem loop ([createBuilderForceAgentsCodingTools](agent-runtime/src/agents/pi-tools.ts)) does NOT yet source its tools from the shared registry (the `NodeCapabilityProvider` + adapter exist but aren't yet driving the live pi loop); and the shared package is source-only (consumed via path alias, no published build/symlink dep), so the Node prod build relies on tsdown resolving the alias — verify on the next agent-runtime build. **(2) Model cascade** — `runCloudToolLoop` treats `proxy.complete()` as binary and terminates on a 429 with `modelStrict:true` ([cloudAgentEngine.ts](api/src/application/runtime/cloudAgentEngine.ts) ~893-935); wrap it in a per-turn retry that drops the strict pin, lets the proxy walk its full chain ([LlmProxyService.ts](api/src/application/llm/LlmProxyService.ts) already cascades), and locks the winning model for later turns (~40 lines, benefits all surfaces — supersedes the observability-only behavior in the model-selection entry below). **(3) Knowledge/memory loop** — reimplement the Node-only [knowledge-loop.ts](agent-runtime/src/infra/knowledge-loop.ts) (disk + SSM `remember()`/`learn()` + WebGPU) Worker-side: a new `task_activity_summaries` table populated in `finalizeCloudRun` (lift `deriveActivitySummary` into a shared package), with prior-activity injected at run start through `getOrSetCached` (L1+L2 KV, invalidated on new-summary write — read-heavy per-run path) and a Vectorize binding as a fast-follow for semantic recall; **SSM `learn()` is the one genuine non-parity** (no in-loop model adaptation on a stateless Worker), mitigated by PRD updates + the builderforce-trained `model.bin` push path. **(4) Orchestration/sub-agents/fleet** — add a service-secret-guarded `POST /api/cloud/dispatch-internal` (reuses `resolveCloudAgent`+`chooseCloudExecutor`+`runCloudToolLoop`) + a Queue binding (none in `wrangler.toml` today) + a `spawn_subagent`/`orchestrate`/`agent_fleet` tool, unifying the local-vs-remote dispatch contract ([remote-subagent.ts](agent-runtime/src/infra/remote-subagent.ts)) across cloud too. **(5) OS-tool parity for the durable surface** — extend `handleContainerOp` with `op=shell`/`op=process` and have the DO surface delegate OS-ops to a **container companion** (per the no-reduction decision) rather than advertising a smaller set — folds in the Worker-has-no-shell residual ([entry on the durable executor below], GAP at [verifyWrittenFiles.ts](api/src/application/repos/verifyWrittenFiles.ts)) and the container HITL/`ask_human` residual. **(6) Retire V1** — only AFTER 1-5 land: backfill `ide_agents.engine`→V2, add `runtime_surface='local'` (extends migration 0105), route On-Prem through the V2 `local` surface, then delete `runV1Engine` + the V1 dispatch branch/label/picker option and drop the vestigial `engine` column (migration 0087). Fixing unblocks: one engine to maintain, identical capabilities on self-hosted and cloud, and deletion of the V1 pi-loop + the three-way tool-list divergence. Gated: parity (1-5) MUST precede V1 deletion (6) or self-hosted regresses from ~40 tools to 7. **✓ Update 2026-06-13 (parity wins + DRY default):** four discrete consolidation gaps closed under the seam (no V1/loop changes): (a) **`ask_human` on on-prem `local`** — `buildNodeCapabilityProvider` takes optional `NodeProviderOptions.{human,webSearch}` and advertises `human`/`web.search` ONLY when wired; the relay `runLocalEngine` injects a `HumanCapability` over the approval-gate (`requestHumanInput` `kind:question` → portal queue); (b) **`web.search` backend** — `web-search.ts` now has a pure `executeWebSearch` reused by BOTH the `web_search` tool and a new `createNodeWebSearch(config)` adapter (DRY), so on-prem `web_search` is live; (c) **local-engine streaming** — `LocalAgentEngine` accepts an optional `LlmStream` (`createGatewayStream` over `nativeStream`) and fires `sinks.onAssistantDelta` → relay `chat.delta` frames; (d) **single default-engine source of truth** — `@builderforce/agent-tools` now exports `ENGINE_IDS`+`DEFAULT_ENGINE_ID`, consumed by relay `resolveEngine`/`task.assign` fallback, cloud `resolveCloudAgent`, and `workforceRoutes` create-default, so the Stage-5 flip is ONE edit. agent-runtime tsgo + api tsc clean; shared-tools + web-search-adapter unit tests green. **✓ Update 2026-06-13 (Stage-5 prerequisite closed):** `runLocalEngine` now builds `buildNodeToolRegistry({ config, workspaceDir, agentDir, sandboxed:false })` WITH the `NodeServiceToolDeps` bag (single hoisted `loadConfig()` — DRY), so on-prem `local` carries the FULL ~40-tool set (service/media/memory) + streaming; Operator decision owed. **UPDATE 2026-06-13 (pass 14) — render SEAM built (the pi-tui replacement's load-bearing half); 18-site migration is the tail:** operator decision — replace `pi-tui` with **`ink` behind a render port**, NOT a raw framework swap, and deliberately NOT a published third-party TUI framework (that is the pi-tui maintenance-asymmetry trap; internal swappability needs only the seam). Net: the pi-tui replacement is now a typed, incremental migration onto a stable seam rather than a big-bang framework swap.

- **Cloudflare account API token was leaked to chat transcript on 2026-05-23.** A real `cfut_*` Workers AI token was pasted as part of a curl example and is now in conversation history (cacheable / loggable on any party that handled the message). The key was never committed to the repo (read from `env.CLOUDFLARE_AI_API_TOKEN` set via `wrangler secret put`), but the leaked token still grants Workers AI quota until rotated on the Cloudflare dashboard (My Profile → API Tokens → roll the existing token). Fixing (rotate the token in the Cloudflare dashboard and `npm run secrets:from-env` after updating `api/.env`) unblocks: confidence that the leaked credential is dead. Mirrors the existing NVIDIA-API-key-leak entry from 2026-05-10 — same playbook.

- **72 React-hooks ergonomics warnings demoted from error to warn.** [frontend/eslint.config.js](frontend/eslint.config.js) downgrades `react-hooks/set-state-in-effect`, `react-hooks/refs`, `react-hooks/purity`, `react-hooks/immutability`, and `react-hooks/preserve-manual-memoization` because `eslint-plugin-react-hooks` v6 + the React Compiler plugin started flagging dozens of legitimate pre-existing patterns (fetch-on-mount, ref-mirror, manual `useCallback`) as errors and broke the deploy. Patterns themselves are not bugs — ergonomics suggestions. Fixing (refactor each warning to the React-Compiler-blessed shape, then re-promote to error) unblocks: catching genuinely-unsafe state mutations during review.

- **`eslint-config-next` is a major version ahead of `next` (16.1.6 vs 15.5.2) — the root cause of the React-Compiler hook-rule wall above.** [frontend/package.json](frontend/package.json) pins `eslint-config-next@16.1.6` against `next@15.5.2`; the v16 config is what enables the React-Compiler-era `react-hooks` rules. The ergonomics rules are demoted to `warn` in [frontend/eslint.config.js](frontend/eslint.config.js), but `react-hooks/rules-of-hooks` correctly stays at error — and that stricter ruleset broke the deploy build a second time via a *false positive*: a plain async event handler named `usePrompt` in [frontend/src/app/prompts/page.tsx](frontend/src/app/prompts/page.tsx) was misclassified as a Hook purely because of its `use` prefix and flagged for being called inside a callback (fixed this pass by renaming to `applyPrompt`). Until the versions are aligned, every future `use`-prefixed non-hook helper will re-trip the same error-level break. Fixing (pin `eslint-config-next` to `15.x` to match `next@15.5.2`, OR deliberately upgrade `next` to 16 and budget the hook-rule refactor) unblocks: a lint ruleset that matches the framework version, and no more naming-driven false-positive build breaks.

- **`requireTenantAccess` unit test uses a hand-rolled Drizzle chain mock.** [api/src/presentation/routes/llmRoutes.test.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/llmRoutes.test.ts) `mockDb()` synthesizes `select().from().where().limit()` chains with canned `[row]` returns. If the auth path grows another link (e.g. `.orderBy`, `.innerJoin`), the mock returns `undefined` and the test still passes while production breaks. Fixing (shared test helper or a real in-memory pg) unblocks: confidence that gateway-auth refactors are caught by tests, not prod.

- **Repo→IDE import is a one-way snapshot capped at 200 files / 5MB, and never clears stale workspace files first.** This pass added "Import to IDE" ([SourceControlContent.tsx](frontend/src/components/sourcecontrol/SourceControlContent.tsx) → `GET /api/repos/repositories/:id/contents`, [importRepoContents.ts](api/src/application/repos/importRepoContents.ts)) so a connected repo hydrates the editable workspace and runs in WebContainer. **Residuals:** (1) caps — a repo with >200 importable files or >5MB of text is partially imported (skips surfaced in the UI as "imported N of M"); full import needs pagination/streaming or the GitHub tarball endpoint. (2) Import **overlays** the existing workspace via `saveFile` without first clearing it, so files from a prior template/import that no longer exist in the repo linger as stale entries. (3) It's **one-way** — there's no "commit IDE edits back to the connected repo" action from the IDE; write-back still relies on the task→PR flow ([openTaskPullRequest.ts](api/src/application/repos/openTaskPullRequest.ts)). (4) ~~GitHub-only~~ **RESOLVED 2026-06-13:** `readRepoFile`/`listRepoFiles` (and therefore the import) now route GitLab/Bitbucket through the shared, tested `RepoSource` (GitHub keeps its inline path → no-regression; +unit tests) — only `searchRepoCode`/`compare` remain GitHub-only (no cross-provider equivalent yet). Fixing the rest unblocks: full-repo, two-way IDE workspaces (caps + overlay-clear + write-back remain).

- **The durable cloud Worker executor can statically validate config but still can't run the project build/type-check/tests in-run (no shell).** `runCloudToolLoop` now has `search_code` (indexed GitHub code search — closed the "blind file-by-file exploration → band-aid edit" failure of exec #52), routes through the curated coding pool, and `run_checks` is now a REAL static validator — it re-parses the agent's committed JSON/YAML config via [verifyWrittenFiles.ts](api/src/application/repos/verifyWrittenFiles.ts) (`JSON.parse` + the runtime `yaml` dep; zero false positives) and blocks a clean finish on a parse error. **Residual (inherent to the shell-less surface):** TS/JS type-checking needs the whole program + node_modules types and tests/build need a shell — neither is possible in a Worker (the `typescript` dep is dev-only; bundling tsc would add ~1MB for *syntax-only* checking and a hand-rolled JS tokenizer would risk false positives that wrongly block agents). So full build/type/test verification stays with CI-on-PR + human review (and the existing webhook CI→auto-fix loop, [ingestRepoCiEvent.ts](api/src/application/ci/ingestRepoCiEvent.ts)). True in-run shell verification needs the long-lived **Container** surface (`run_command`, future infra) or routing V2 to the agent-runtime Claude Agent SDK loop with a sandbox. Fixing that unblocks: V2 cloud agents that type-check/test before shipping, not just config-validate. Related to the "Cloud agents wired but only happy-path validated" entry above.

- **Migration `0098_task_specs_and_spec_status.sql` not yet applied to any live DB.** The Product-Management PRD feature (task↔PRD many-to-many via `task_specs`, destructive `spec_status` enum swap `reviewed/approved→ready`, `done→complete`, and `DROP COLUMN tasks.spec_id`) is implemented, type-checks, and passes all 488 api tests + drift check, but the migration is a destructive enum swap + column drop and was deliberately NOT auto-run against the operator's Neon DB. Running it (`npm --prefix api run db:migrate` against the intended dev DB, then verify `\d+ specs` shows the new enum, `\d task_specs` exists, `tasks` has no `spec_id`, backfill count == prior `COUNT(*) WHERE spec_id IS NOT NULL`, then re-run for idempotency) unblocks: the whole feature going live. Note the partial unique index `uq_task_specs_primary ON task_specs(task_id) WHERE is_primary` is migration-only (the drift checker doesn't track partial indexes) — confirm it exists post-apply.

- **Stub detection has a hard static-analysis ceiling: a byte-valid stub is indistinguishable from real code.** The anti-stub finish gate ([scanWrittenForPlaceholders](api/src/application/repos/scanForPlaceholders.ts), wired into `finish` in [cloudAgentEngine.ts](api/src/application/runtime/cloudAgentEngine.ts)) now catches both the announced stubs (`// In a real …`, `assuming … exists`, `mock <noun>`, bracketed `[Platform Name]`, `replace with actual`) AND the silent structural ones (empty typed function body, `throw new Error('not implemented')`, `return null as Foo`, `// TODO`/`FIXME`, hard-coded `@example.com` / `your-api-key` literals) — paired with the `delete_file` tool and the prior-branch-diff context so dead code is both detectable and removable. **Irreducible residual:** a stub that is *syntactically valid, comment-free, and returns a plausible hard-coded value* (e.g. `return "BuilderForce"` standing in for a real lookup, or a `return null;` that reads exactly like a legitimate guard) cannot be told apart from correct code by any static check without crossing into false positives — that is a model-quality problem, not a detector gap, and it folds into the **"Routing pools are hand-maintained"** entry above (route coding tasks off the weak free-pool tail, e.g. `gemini-2.5-flash-lite`, so they aren't generated in the first place). No further detector work is warranted; closing it lives in model routing.

- **Standup/Planning round-table ceremony shipped (live multiplayer + Epic/sprint drag); five residuals.** This pass built a reusable [CeremonyStage](frontend/src/components/ceremony/CeremonyStage.tsx) (round table of human+agent seats; drag a backlog ticket onto a seat to assign, onto an Epic to group, onto the sprint bar to schedule, onto the center to mark Done) available both as a dedicated route ([/ceremonies](frontend/src/app/ceremonies/page.tsx) + sidebar nav) and a full-screen overlay from the Tasks board ([TaskMgmtContent.tsx](frontend/src/components/TaskMgmtContent.tsx) "Start standup/planning"). Live multiplayer via a new [CeremonyRoomDO](api/src/infrastructure/relay/CeremonyRoomDO.ts) (presence + cursor + `changed` relay, keyed `ceremony:<projectId>`, bound `CEREMONY_ROOM` / migration tag v7) and the [useCeremonyRoom](frontend/src/lib/ceremonyRoom.ts) hook. Full Epic support: PATCH/POST `/api/tasks` now accept `taskType`/`parentTaskId`/`sprintId` ([taskRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/taskRoutes.ts) → [TaskService](api/src/application/task/TaskService.ts) → [TaskRepository](api/src/infrastructure/repositories/TaskRepository.ts)), the task↔sprint link is migration [0115](api/migrations/0115_sprint_task_assignment.sql) (`tasks.sprint_id` FK, ON DELETE SET NULL), and the frontend [Task](frontend/src/lib/builderforceApi.ts) type + `tasksApi.tree/decompose` + `sprintsApi` are exposed. The `broadcastRoom` helper was extracted to a [shared module](api/src/infrastructure/relay/broadcastRoom.ts) (DRY with poker/retro) and the assignee encode/decode helpers to [lib/taskAssignee.ts](frontend/src/lib/taskAssignee.ts). **Residuals:** (1) **Migration 0115 not yet applied to a live DB** — schema-drift check + 646 api tests pass, but `tasks.sprint_id` must be added by running `npm --prefix api run db:migrate` against the dev DB (verify the column + `idx_tasks_sprint`, re-run for idempotency). (2) **Presence identity is self-reported** by the client's `join` frame — the DO does not re-verify the JWT per frame (the WS upgrade itself is auth-gated under `/api/agile`); server-stamped identity is a follow-up. (3) **`changed` propagation is client-driven** — broadcast on local-mutation success, so a peer who mutates while disconnected won't notify others; a server-authoritative broadcast from `taskRoutes` after PATCH would close this. (4) **Ceremonies are ephemeral** (room == project; no persisted standup/planning session history, no retro/poker integration). (5) **No DnD-library affordances** — native HTML5 drag has no drop-preview ghost/keyboard a11y, and the seat in-flight stacks (standup) can overlap when many members ring a small table; a future pass could switch to dnd-kit or cap/auto-layout the ellipse. The task detail in the ceremony is a lightweight read-only panel that links back to the full board drawer (the board's rich `renderTaskCard`/drawer wasn't extracted — see the related Epic-decomposition board-tree-UI residual). Fixing unblocks: governed, persistent ceremonies with server-trusted presence and a unified task card across board + table.

- **Ceremony tracking + scorecards + power meters shipped (Phase 2); reconciled with the parallel member-metrics effort.** Ceremonies are now *measured*: migration [0119](api/migrations/0119_ceremony_sessions.sql) (renamed from a colliding `0116` — the parallel effort had already taken 0116/0117/0118) adds `ceremony_sessions` + `ceremony_participants` and board-level `standup_turn_mode`/`standup_turn_seconds`; [ceremonyRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/ceremonyRoutes.ts) gains session CRUD (`GET /sessions`, `POST /sessions`, `PATCH /sessions/:id/turn`, `POST /sessions/:id/complete`, all MANAGER+). API 653 tests + frontend 218 tests pass. **Residuals:** (1) **Migrations 0115 + 0116–0119 not yet applied to a live DB** — schema-drift check passes; run `npm --prefix api run db:migrate` and verify the new tables/columns. (2) **Auto-dispatch on Complete is client-driven** (facilitator's browser submits the runs) — a disconnect mid-Complete drops some runs; server-side dispatch from `POST /sessions/:id/complete` is the hardening follow-up. (3) **Scorecard cache is TTL-only** (the parallel `/api/members/metrics` cache); ceremony adds no write-invalidation. (4) **Turn timing is wall-clock from `turn_started_at`** — no pause/resume; a tab closed mid-turn over-counts until the next advance/complete. (5) **Power-meter cap falls back to a soft constant (8)** when a member has no `member_profiles` row. (6) **Human/host specialization, success-rate, latency, rating** remain "No data yet" where the member-metrics system has no signal (cloud-agent-rich, human-sparse by design).

- **`orchestrate` tool's planning push is not task-linked — tool-side plumbing DONE, but no `taskId` SOURCE in the session context.** [orchestrate-tool.ts](agent-runtime/src/builderforce/tools/orchestrate-tool.ts) now accepts a `taskId` option and forwards it to `pushSpec` (links the PRD as the task's primary) [1277]. **Real remaining blocker (deeper than the original entry assumed):** the construction context has no taskId to pass — `createBuilderForceAgentsTools`/`BuilderForceAgentsToolsOptions` carry agent-session fields but NO `taskId` (host-side `/spec` orchestration runs in a general agent session, not a per-task dispatch). - **"Project integration keys" section has no edit / token-rotate UI.** This pass added repository edit (key-switch), a per-repo "Test" accessibility probe (`POST /api/repos/repositories/:id/test` via [resolveRepoCredential](api/src/application/repos/resolveRepoCredential.ts)), and edit/remove icons to [SourceControlContent.tsx](frontend/src/components/sourcecontrol/SourceControlContent.tsx); it also wired `credentialId` into the Brain `repos.add`/`repos.update` capabilities ([platformActions.ts](frontend/src/lib/brain/platformActions.ts)) so a key switch is no longer silently dropped, and coerced `credentialId: '' → null` in the repo PATCH/POST so an empty selection clears the uuid FK instead of failing and "reverting". **Still missing:** [IntegrationCredentialsManager](frontend/src/components/integrations/IntegrationCredentialsManager.tsx) (the "Project integration keys" card) exposes only Test/Delete/Add — no edit to rename a key or rotate its secret, even though `integrationsApi.update` + the backend `PATCH /api/integrations/:id` already support both. - **First-party server-side MCP server covers projects + tasks only — other domains not yet wired.** A built-in MCP server now exposes platform capabilities in-process through the gateway ([api/src/application/llm/builtinMcpService.ts](api/src/application/llm/builtinMcpService.ts), merged into `GET /v1/mcp/tools` + dispatched in `POST /v1/mcp/call` under the `builtin` extension id in [llmRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/llmRoutes.ts)), so external/headless MCP clients and the agent-runtime can call platform actions, not just the browser Brain (which skips the `builtin` set via [McpExtensionsBridge](frontend/src/components/brain/McpExtensionsBridge.tsx) since it has the richer client manifest). **Full READ parity 2026-06-13:** `CATALOG` now exposes EVERY named domain server-side via tenant-scoped `ctx.db` queries — projects, tasks (full CRUD via services), plus **workflows** (list/get), **specs/PRDs** (list/get), **prompts** (list), **approvals** (list), **agents** (list), **boards** (list), **cron** (list) [1296] (+unit test asserting all advertise). Deliberately NOT done as raw `ctx.db` writes — those would bypass each domain's validation/business rules; doing it right means routing each write through that domain's service/repo with a tenant guard (extract a thin service where none exists). Read consumers (headless/cron discovery) have full parity now; write parity is the remaining per-domain service work.

- **No CI step runs `db:migrate` against an ephemeral DB before deploy — missing-`CREATE` schema drift only surfaces in production.** This pass fixed a hard production-deploy crash (`relation "contributors" does not exist`) caused by the entire contributor/team/report/team-memory subsystem (schema sections 6b–6f) being defined in [schema.ts](api/src/infrastructure/database/schema.ts) and wired into routes ([analyticsRoutes](api/src/presentation/routes/analyticsRoutes.ts), [contributorRoutes](api/src/presentation/routes/contributorRoutes.ts), the P4-5 team-memory mesh) but never given a `CREATE TABLE` migration — the tables only ever existed locally via `drizzle-kit push`. Migration 0056's `to_regclass()` guards silently no-op'd against the absent tables, masking the drift until 0069 ALTERed `contributors` unguarded. New migration [0068a_create_contributor_team_subsystem.sql](api/migrations/0068a_create_contributor_team_subsystem.sql) backfills the creates (idempotent, post-0056/pre-0069 shape, also creates the `activity_event_type`/`report_type`/`report_schedule` enums that were likewise never created). The remaining gap: the `db:migrate` job in [.github/workflows](.github/workflows) applies migrations straight to the production Neon branch with no prior dry-run, and [check-schema-drift.mjs](api/scripts/check-schema-drift.mjs) is not gated in CI to catch a schema-table that has no creating migration. Fixing (a CI job that spins a throwaway Neon branch or local Postgres, runs `db:migrate` from empty + then `check-schema-drift.mjs`, and fails the build on either error before the deploy job runs) unblocks: missing-migration / drift bugs caught in PR instead of as a prod deploy crash. NOTE: `team_memory` (the cross-claw mesh) was among the silently-uncreated tables, so that feature was non-functional in any push-free environment until 0068a.

- **The `pgTable`-block regex in [check-schema-drift.mjs](api/scripts/check-schema-drift.mjs) was merging adjacent tables — now fixed, but exposed `claw_skill_assignments` as a push-only table.** The drift checker's table-capture regex (`...\n\}\)`) could not close a `}, (t) => [ ... ]` constraints block, so it ran past the closing brace and swallowed the *next* table's declaration under the first table's name — fabricating ~96 phantom column entries in [.schema-drift-allowlist.txt](api/scripts/.schema-drift-allowlist.txt) (e.g. `dev_team_members.report_type`/`.delivery_hour`/`.recipients`, which are really `report_schedules` columns; `report_subscriptions.claw_id`/`.summary`, which are `team_memory` columns). This pass fixed the regex (`\n\}\s*[,)]` — close on `}` followed by `)` or `,`) and rebuilt the allowlist down to the 110 genuinely-grandfathered push-only entries (parsed-table coverage rose to all 142). The fix un-hid [clawSkillAssignments](api/src/infrastructure/database/schema.ts) — the claw-scoped sibling of `tenant_skill_assignments` — which, like its sibling and the whole base cluster (`tenants`, `users`, `coderclaw_instances`, `marketplace_skills`, `projects`, `tasks`, `executions`), has **no `CREATE TABLE` migration** yet is queried unguarded at runtime ([skillAssignmentRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/skillAssignmentRoutes.ts), [clawRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/clawRoutes.ts)) — the same `relation "X" does not exist` prod-crash class 0068a fixed for the contributor cluster. It was grandfathered (matching its sibling) rather than migrated, since converting it alone while leaving its push-only FK targets (`coderclaw_instances`, `marketplace_skills`) un-migrated would be inconsistent. Fixing (a `0073`-style idempotent `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` migration that converts the whole push-only baseline cluster — base tables + both skill-assignment tables — to tracked migrations, then dropping their allowlist entries) unblocks: skill assignment + base CRUD working in any push-free environment, and shrinking the grandfather list toward zero.

- **[ROUTABLE SIGNAL DONE 2026-06-13] `/models` catalog — pricing-context + admin-invalidate residuals only.** Part (a) shipped [1305]: each `CatalogModel` is annotated `routable` + `pool: 'free'|'pro'` computed from the curated vendor catalog (`catalogEntry` in [modelCatalog.ts](api/src/application/llm/modelCatalog.ts), +unit test), and the Models page surfaces it as a "✓ Routable" chip, a "Routable" field/column, and a "Routable only" filter ([ModelsPageClient.tsx](frontend/src/app/models/ModelsPageClient.tsx) + [modelCatalog.ts](frontend/src/lib/modelCatalog.ts)) — a visitor now sees which models the cascade actually serves. **Residual:** (b) the per-1M pricing is still OpenRouter's verbatim point-in-time number with no effective-rate/markup context; (c) no admin "invalidate catalog cache" button (it ages out on the 1h KV TTL) — a manual `invalidateCached(env, 'openrouter-catalog:v1')` action would force-refresh after an upstream pricing change.

- **[DONE 2026-06-18] frontend now consumes the engine via the `@seanhogg/builderforce-memory-engine` npm package, not the `mambacode.js` git URL.** [frontend/package.json](frontend/package.json) now depends on `@seanhogg/builderforce-memory-engine@^2026.6.19`; [frontend/src/lib/model-provider.ts](frontend/src/lib/model-provider.ts) imports (static type + dynamic) from it; the redundant `declare module 'mambacode.js'` shim was dropped from [frontend/global.d.ts](frontend/global.d.ts) (the npm package ships its own types). The WebGPU `MambaModel`/`MambaTrainer`/`BPETokenizer`/`initWebGPU` exports resolve and `tsc --noEmit` passes with 0 errors; model-provider tests green (19/19). The browser training path now rides the canonical npm package instead of a moving git HEAD.

- **`boards.autonomous` column is now inert.** The Board-settings Autonomous checkbox was removed this pass ([BoardConfigPanel SettingsTab](frontend/src/components/board/BoardConfigPanel.tsx)) and the coordinator no longer reads `board.autonomous` — autonomy is implicit (a successful stage advances unless the lane gate is `human`; see [resolveStageAction](api/src/application/swimlane/transitions.ts)). The `boards.autonomous` column ([schema.ts](api/src/infrastructure/database/schema.ts)) is left in place (defaulted `true`, board-create forces `true`) to avoid a destructive migration, but nothing reads it. Fixing (drop the column + its `BoardLite.autonomous` field + the `getBoard` mapping once confirmed no reader remains) unblocks: dead-column cleanup.

- **`telemetry_spans` had no `CREATE TABLE` migration — fixed in 0073; `agents` + `approval_rules` remain push-only.** Same drift class as 0068a (contributor cluster) and the `0073`-style note above: [telemetrySpans](api/src/infrastructure/database/schema.ts) was declared in schema.ts and queried unguarded by [GET /api/analytics/activity-calendar](api/src/presentation/routes/analyticsRoutes.ts), but only ever existed via the `drizzle-kit push` baseline — no tracked migration created it, and 0056's `to_regclass()` guard silently no-op'd its `segment_id` block against the absent table. Production (migration-only provisioning) 500'd with `relation "telemetry_spans" does not exist`. Closed this pass by [0073_telemetry_spans_table.sql](api/migrations/0073_telemetry_spans_table.sql) (idempotent `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` matching schema.ts, replaying 0056's `segment_id` column + default-fill trigger + `NOT NULL` + index since 0056 runs first and skipped it) and dropping the `telemetry_spans.*` rows from [.schema-drift-allowlist.txt](api/scripts/.schema-drift-allowlist.txt). **Tables now tracked (closed):** `agents` + `approval_rules` got their idempotent migration [0123_agents_and_approval_rules_tables.sql](api/migrations/0123_agents_and_approval_rules_tables.sql) (same 0073 template — guarded enum create + replayed 0056 segment_id trigger/NOT NULL/index) and their 18 allowlist rows were dropped (drift now grandfathers 75, was 93). **Residual:** gating [check-schema-drift.mjs](api/scripts/check-schema-drift.mjs) in CI (per the 0068a entry) so drift is caught at PR time, not prod — still open.

- **Native client apps were migrated into [apps/](apps/) as raw source but are not branded or CI-wired.** This pass consolidated the Android/iOS/macOS/shared clients (627 tracked files) out of the now-archived `SeanHogg/BuilderForceAgents` repo (the renamed-and-deprecated `coderClaw` repo) into [apps/](apps/), closing the "native apps have no home in Builderforce.ai" gap. **Still deferred:** (a) ~445 of those files still carry `coderclaw` branding, including the Android package namespace `ai.coderclaw.android` ([apps/android/app/build.gradle.kts](apps/android/app/build.gradle.kts), [AndroidManifest.xml](apps/android/app/src/main/AndroidManifest.xml) and the whole `java/ai/coderclaw/android/**` tree), iOS/macos bundle ids, and in-app copy — none rewritten to the BuilderForce brand; (b) the apps are standalone gradle/xcode projects with no entry in any Builderforce.ai build/CI pipeline (the repo has no root `pnpm-workspace.yaml`/`package.json`), so they are parked source that nothing builds, tests, or releases; (c) `apps/ios/fastlane/.env.example` had to be force-added past the root `.gitignore` `.env.*` rule — fine for a template, but the fastlane signing/release flow it documents is not connected to any pipeline here. Fixing (rename the `ai.coderclaw.*` namespaces + bundle ids to the BuilderForce brand via a one-shot codemod, then add a native-build CI job — gradle assemble + xcodebuild — and decide the release/appcast path now that [appcast.xml](appcast.xml) for the macOS app no longer lives beside the runtime) unblocks: shippable, brand-consistent native clients instead of archived-repo source parked in-tree. Related to the agent-runtime lobster/brand-sweep entry above — same "consolidated deployable still wears the old brand" root cause.

- **Agent API-key prefix migration `clk_`→`bfa_` is half-done (dual-accept live; legacy keys not yet rotated/dropped).** New BuilderForce Agents are now minted as `bfa_*` ([agentHostRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/agentHostRoutes.ts) `generateApiKey('bfa')`) and auth accepts BOTH `bfa_`/`clk_` ([llmRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/llmRoutes.ts)), so no new credential carries the retired "claw" brand and existing `clk_` keys keep working. **Remaining:** (a) rotate already-issued `clk_*` keys to `bfa_*`, then delete the `clk_` acceptance branch + the `'clk'` cache-namespace string ([keyResolutionCache.ts](api/src/infrastructure/auth/keyResolutionCache.ts)) once none remain; (b) the **`clu_`** legacy user-bootstrap key ([HashService.ts](api/src/infrastructure/auth/HashService.ts), minted in [AuthService.ts](api/src/application/auth/AuthService.ts)) is also a `cl*` brand remnant — rename under the same dual-accept playbook if still in use. Fixing unblocks: zero "claw" in any credential prefix.

- **`cosineSimilarity` is duplicated in the gateway (can't import the WebGPU library into a Worker).** [`api/src/application/llm/semanticCache.ts`](api/src/application/llm/semanticCache.ts) carries a local copy of the cosine maths that also lives in `@builderforce/memory`'s `similarity` module, because importing the memory package would drag the WebGPU engine into the Worker bundle. - **Agent-produced PR is recorded in `pull_requests` but never surfaced on the kanban card or anywhere in the frontend.** [RepoService.recordPrResult](api/src/application/repos/RepoService.ts) updates the `pull_requests` row (number/url/status) but does NOT write the resulting URL back onto `tasks.githubPrUrl`, and the frontend never calls the `GET /api/repos/projects/:projectId/pull-requests` list endpoint ([repoRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/repoRoutes.ts)) — `builderforceApi.ts` has no repos/PR client. The only PR link shown on a card ([TaskMgmtContent.tsx:634](frontend/src/components/TaskMgmtContent.tsx) / drawer :1215) comes from the manually-typed `githubPrUrl` form field, so an autonomously-created PR is invisible until a human pastes the link. Fixing (write `githubPrUrl` back onto the task in `recordPrResult`, OR add a repos/PR client + a "PRs / changes" tab that reads the pull-requests list) unblocks: closing the agent→visible-change loop without manual copy-paste. This is the "code changes are tracked and you can see what the cloud agent changed" requirement — backend records it, frontend does not display it.

- **Two cron patterns coexist now.** [/api/approvals/escalate](api/src/presentation/routes/approvalRoutes.ts) is HTTP-triggered with a `CRON_SECRET` query param (requires an external scheduler to hit the URL), while [vendor health probe](api/src/index.ts) uses the native Cloudflare `scheduled()` handler + `[triggers] crons` block in [api/wrangler.toml](api/wrangler.toml). The native handler is the right pattern on Workers — it has no public surface to abuse and doesn't depend on an external scheduler. Fixing (migrate `escalate` into `scheduled()` alongside the vendor probe, drop the `CRON_SECRET` route) unblocks: single cron pattern, one less public endpoint.

- **Schema-drift allowlist contains 106 pre-existing drift items.** [api/scripts/.schema-drift-allowlist.txt](api/scripts/.schema-drift-allowlist.txt) grandfathers 106 columns/tables that exist in [schema.ts](api/src/infrastructure/database/schema.ts) without a tracked migration — they were likely created via `drizzle-kit push` rather than a versioned migration. - **The no-bleed invariants have no repeatable DB-backed test — only the resolver + provisioning logic are unit-tested.** Covered by unit tests: [resolveSegment](api/src/infrastructure/auth/segmentResolver.test.ts) (tenant-scoped default/federated/cache) and [segmentRoutes](api/src/presentation/routes/segmentRoutes.test.ts) (tenant-stamped provisioning, no `isolation_mode` escalation, default/cross-tenant PATCH guard). They were verified once by hand at migration time but nothing locks them. Fixing (a DB-backed integration test — ephemeral Postgres or a gated Neon test branch — that inserts for a single tenant and asserts the fill, flips a throwaway tenant to `segmented` and asserts the insert is rejected, and once RLS lands asserts a Segment-A context cannot SELECT Segment-B rows) unblocks: regression-proofing the core hard rule instead of relying on a one-time manual check.

- **Twelve business tables are absent from the database (legacy `drizzle-kit push` debt) so 0056 skipped them.** `activity_events`, `approval_rules`, `contributor_daily_metrics`, `contributor_identities`, `contributors`, `dev_teams`, `integration_credentials`, `integration_sync_logs`, `report_schedules`, `report_subscriptions`, `team_memory`, `telemetry_spans` are declared in [schema.ts](api/src/infrastructure/database/schema.ts) and grandfathered in [.schema-drift-allowlist.txt](api/scripts/.schema-drift-allowlist.txt) but have no `CREATE TABLE` migration and do not exist in this DB; 0056's `to_regclass` guard skipped them, so their `segment_id` (+ trigger) is unapplied where they don't exist and their features are already non-functional in this environment. - **The root (frontend/studio/brain) test suite has 28 failing tests — pre-existing, unrelated to the API.** Running `npx vitest run` from the repo root (vs `api/`) reports 28 failures across [frontend/src/lib/api.test.ts](frontend/src/lib/api.test.ts) + [auth.test.ts](frontend/src/lib/auth.test.ts) (`window is not defined` — jsdom environment not set for those files), and `studio-embedded` / `brain-embedded` `*.test.tsx` (`RolldownError: Parse failure` on TSX). - **Governance/Security pillar COMPLETE for the ported toolset — 9 surfaces live end-to-end.** Shipped + verified (api 130 tests, drift 75 tables, all tsc 0): schema [0057](api/migrations/0057_governance_compliance.sql) + [0058](api/migrations/0058_governance_trackers.sql) (SOC2 controls/evidence, vendors, incidents, PII inventory, DPAs, trainings, compliance events, DSR, suppression — all `(tenant_id, segment_id)`-scoped with the 0056 trigger); the **fully Segment-THREADED** [governanceRoutes](api/src/presentation/routes/governanceRoutes.ts) (`/api/governance/soc2/*` bespoke + a DRY `createTrackerRoutes` factory mounted for the 8 trackers — every read+write scoped by `(tenantId, segmentId)` from context, 12 tests); frontend [Soc2Content](frontend/src/components/governance/Soc2Content.tsx) + ONE generic [TrackerSurface](frontend/src/components/governance/TrackerSurface.tsx) driven by [trackerConfigs](frontend/src/components/governance/trackerConfigs.ts), all wired (`available:true`). **13 embed views now live** (Product: ideas/prd/backlog; Agile: kanban; Security: soc2 + 8 trackers). **Still open in Security:** (a) DevSecOps surfaces `access-reviews` + `vuln-scans` (doc 07 SEC-8/9) — deferred, they need Repo connection + scan/agent integration, not simple CRUD; (b) `security_audit_log` writes on every governance mutation (doc 07 §3/§4); (c) SOC 2 evidence-attach UI + JSON export (API exists). - **The Product/Agile trackers are standalone CRUD, not yet linked to the `work_items` spine or to each other.** E.g. a `sprint` row and `feature-scoring` row don't reference shared work items; `mvp`/`roadmap`/`release` aren't linked. - **The frontend's `@seanhogg/builderforce-embedded` must be a real junction, not a copy — and the embed package must be pre-built.** On this Windows/MSYS host `ln -s` COPIED the package dir into `frontend/node_modules/@seanhogg/builderforce-embedded`, so a package rebuild didn't propagate and the frontend type-checked against stale types until the copy was replaced with a `mklink /J` junction. A clean checkout / CI must (a) run the workspace install so the `link:` dep becomes a proper junction, and (b) `cd builderforce-embedded && npm run build` before `next build`, since the frontend imports the built `dist`. Fixing (a root install+build step that links + builds the embedded packages, mirroring studio/brain) unblocks: reproducible builds where embed-package changes are actually seen by the frontend.
